### [] assistant

数据够了，直接给你结论：

---

## Kejilion.sh 调研结论

**本质**：一个**一键脚本工具箱**，运行在服务器终端里，一个 bash 脚本集成几十种服务器管理功能。

官方命令：

```bash
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh)
```

---

### 它能做什么

| 类别 | 具体功能 |
|------|----------|
| **系统管理** | 系统信息、更新维护、性能优化、Swap 创建、时区同步 |
| **Docker** | 容器管理、镜像部署、Docker 一键安装 |
| **网站部署** | LNMP 建站、SSL 证书申请、域名绑定、反向代理 |
| **网络工具** | BBR 加速、WARP 管理、FRP 客户端/服务端、负载均衡 |
| **安全** | 防火墙规则、国家 IP 黑名单、DDoS 防御、SSH 加固 |
| **数据库** | MySQL/PostgreSQL 安装调优 |

---

### 关键发现

**优点：**

- 一站式，不需要记多个脚本；
- 有中文菜单，交互友好；
- 功能覆盖日常服务器管理的核心场景；
- 支持大多数主流 Linux 发行版。

**潜在问题：**

1. ** telemetry（遥测）**：脚本里有 `send_stats` 函数，会收集使用功能、IP、国家、CPU 架构等 anonymized 数据。虽然作者声明不收集敏感信息，但这个机制客观存在；
2. **依赖 gh.kejilion.pro 镜像**：脚本根据 IP 自动选择源，如果你的 VPS 是 Oracle Cloud 美西，会走 GitHub raw 源，不走镜像；
3. **锦灯笼社区版 vs 官方版**：这个脚本有社区修改版在流通，来源需要确认。

---

### 对你这台 Oracle VPS 的价值

**有用的：**

```bash
# 安全加固
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh)     # 进入菜单，找防火墙/SSH加固

# BBR3 加速
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh) bbr3

# Docker 一键安装
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh) docker

# 反向代理（如果你要建网站）
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh) fd
```

**不建议用它做的：**

- 防火墙规则（你只有一台 VPS，自己用 ufw 更可控）；
- 数据库安装（你已经知道 Oracle 3306/5432 暴露公网的问题，先堵上再说）；
- WARP（Oracle Cloud IP 本身已经被 AI 服务识别，WARP 也救不了）。

---

### 我的建议

**不要用 Kejilion.sh 替代你自己配置 VPS 的过程**，原因：

1. 你现在的 VPS 最大的问题是**端口太开**，先用 ufw 关掉 MySQL/PostgreSQL 的公网访问，这个不需要脚本；
2. Kejilion.sh 适合**快速搭建网站/博客**的场景，你不一定是这个需求；
3. 它的 SSL 证书、反代、LNMP 这些功能，是给建站用的，不是给你做 AI 基础设施用的。

**真正适合你用的场景：**

```bash
# 一键 BBR3 加速（有用）
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh) bbr3

# Docker 安装（有用，以后可能用到）
bash <(curl -sL kejilion.sh) docker
```

---

### 你现在真正应该做的事

先用**纯 ufw** 做安全加固，比用 Kejilion.sh 更干净：

```bash
# 登录到 VPS 后一条条执行
sudo ufw delete allow 3306
sudo ufw delete allow 5432
sudo ufw delete allow 8888
sudo ufw allow 22222/tcp    # 你的新SSH端口
sudo ufw allow 443/tcp
sudo ufw allow 80/tcp
sudo ufw reload
sudo ufw status
```

Kejilion.sh 可以当作**补充工具**，在你熟悉了基础操作后，用它快速跑 BBR3 / Docker 安装这些高频操作。

---

**要不要我直接给你一套 ufw 加固 + BBR3 + Docker 的具体步骤？** 或者你想先继续研究 Kejilion.sh 有什么别的想用的功能？

### [] user

Review the conversation above and update the skill library. Be ACTIVE — most sessions produce at least one skill update, even if small. A pass that does nothing is a missed learning opportunity, not a neutral outcome.

Target shape of the library: CLASS-LEVEL skills, each with a rich SKILL.md and a `references/` directory for session-specific detail. Not a long flat list of narrow one-session-one-skill entries. This shapes HOW you update, not WHETHER you update.

Signals to look for (any one of these warrants action):
  • User corrected your style, tone, format, legibility, or verbosity. Frustration signals like 'stop doing X', 'this is too verbose', 'don't format like this', 'why are you explaining', 'just give me the answer', 'you always do Y and I hate it', or an explicit 'remember this' are FIRST-CLASS skill signals, not just memory signals. Update the relevant skill(s) to embed the preference so the next session starts already knowing.
  • User corrected your workflow, approach, or sequence of steps. Encode the correction as a pitfall or explicit step in the skill that governs that class of task.
  • Non-trivial technique, fix, workaround, debugging path, or tool-usage pattern emerged that a future session would benefit from. Capture it.
  • A skill that got loaded or consulted this session turned out to be wrong, missing a step, or outdated. Patch it NOW.

Preference order — prefer the earliest action that fits, but do pick one when a signal above fired:
  1. UPDATE A CURRENTLY-LOADED SKILL. Look back through the conversation for skills the user loaded via /skill-name or you read via skill_view. If any of them covers the territory of the new learning, PATCH that one first. It is the skill that was in play, so it's the right one to extend.
  2. UPDATE AN EXISTING UMBRELLA (via skills_list + skill_view). If no loaded skill fits but an existing class-level skill does, patch it. Add a subsection, a pitfall, or broaden a trigger.
  3. ADD A SUPPORT FILE under an existing umbrella. Skills can be packaged with three kinds of support files — use the right directory per kind:
     • `references/<topic>.md` — session-specific detail (error transcripts, reproduction recipes, provider quirks) AND condensed knowledge banks: quoted research, API docs, external authoritative excerpts, or domain notes you found while working on the problem. Write it concise and for the value of the task, not as a full mirror of upstream docs.
     • `templates/<name>.<ext>` — starter files meant to be copied and modified (boilerplate configs, scaffolding, a known-good example the agent can `reproduce with modifications`).
     • `scripts/<name>.<ext>` — statically re-runnable actions the skill can invoke directly (verification scripts, fixture generators, deterministic probes, anything the agent should run rather than hand-type each time).
     Add support files via skill_manage action=write_file with file_path starting 'references/', 'templates/', or 'scripts/'. The umbrella's SKILL.md should gain a one-line pointer to any new support file so future agents know it exists.
  4. CREATE A NEW CLASS-LEVEL UMBRELLA SKILL when no existing skill covers the class. The name MUST be at the class level. The name MUST NOT be a specific PR number, error string, feature codename, library-alone name, or 'fix-X / debug-Y / audit-Z-today' session artifact. If the proposed name only makes sense for today's task, it's wrong — fall back to (1), (2), or (3).

User-preference embedding (important): when the user expressed a style/format/workflow preference, the update belongs in the SKILL.md body, not just in memory. Memory captures 'who the user is and what the current situation and state of your operations are'; skills capture 'how to do this class of task for this user'. When they complain about how you handled a task, the skill that governs that task needs to carry the lesson.

If you notice two existing skills that overlap, note it in your reply — the background curator handles consolidation at scale.

'Nothing to save.' is a real option but should NOT be the default. If the session ran smoothly with no corrections and produced no new technique, just say 'Nothing to save.' and stop. Otherwise, act.

美国-手动\n    - 美国-自动\n\n美国-手动:\n  type: select\n  use: [Mitce, 花云]\n  filter: \"(?i)(美国|US|United States|...)\"\n```\n\nUsing `use:` limits ordinary regional groups to subscription providers and excludes static scarce exits.\n\n## Fallback behavior the user likes\n\nThe user explicitly prefers this behavior:\n\n1. default to manually selected regional node;\n2. if manual node is down, fail over to auto-tested regional node;\n3. when manual node recovers, switch back to manual.\n\nImplement as:\n\n```yaml\n美国-故转:\n  type: fallback\n  proxies:\n    - 美国-手动\n    - 美国-自动\n  lazy: false\n  interval: 300\n```\n\n## Rule-provider verification findings\n\nVerified examples that returned HTTP 200 during the session:\n\n- `blackmatrix7/.../OpenAI/OpenAI.list`\n- `blackmatrix7/.../Claude/Claude.list`\n- `blackmatrix7/.../PayPal/PayPal.list`\n- `blackmatrix7/.../Stripe/Stripe.list`\n- `blackmatrix7/.../UBI/UBI.list`\n- `blackmatrix7/.../Steam/Steam.list`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geosite/openai.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geosite/tiktok.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geosite/netflix.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geoip/google.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geoip/telegram.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/meta-rules-dat/meta/geo/geoip/netflix.mrs`\n\nExamples that returned 404 and should not be used without re-checking:\n\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geoip/tiktok.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geoip/github.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geoip/microsoft.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geoip/steam.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geosite/gemini.mrs`\n- `MetaCubeX/.../geosite/copilot.mrs`\n\n## Scenario routing decisions\n\n- AI high-risk: fixed US landing first; regular US fallback.\n- AI ordinary: regular US/JP/SG, no scarce landing.\n- Payment: fixed US landing first, because volume is low and identity stability matters.\n- Crypto exchanges: SG/HK/JP first; avoid US first because exchange region restrictions can be worse than IP-quality benefits.\n- TikTok: JP/SG/US only by default; avoid countries where service operation/content region is unreliable.\n- UBI: TW first if the user reports Ubisoft server is Taiwan; US fallback.\n- Steam: US first, JP/SG fallback.\n- Video: region unlock groups, never scarce landing.\n", "file_type": ".md"}

{"success": true, "name": "networking/openclash-scenario-routing", "file": "scripts/validate_openclash_yaml.py", "content": "#!/usr/bin/env python3\n\"\"\"Validate an OpenClash/Mihomo YAML for common reference mistakes.\n\nChecks:\n- YAML parses\n- every RULE-SET provider exists\n- every rule target exists as a proxy group or static proxy\n- every proxy-group `proxies:` reference exists\n\nUsage:\n  python3 validate_openclash_yaml.py /path/to/config.yaml\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport sys\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom typing import Any\n\nimport yaml\n\n\ndef main(path: str) -> int:\n    p = Path(path)\n    data: dict[str, Any] = yaml.safe_load(p.read_text(encoding=\"utf-8\"))\n\n    groups = {g[\"name\"] for g in data.get(\"proxy-groups\", []) if isinstance(g, dict) and \"name\" in g}\n    proxies = {x[\"name\"] for x in data.get(\"proxies\", []) if isinstance(x, dict) and \"name\" in x}\n    proxies |= {\"DIRECT\", \"REJECT\", \"直连\", \"拒绝\"}\n    providers = set((data.get(\"rule-providers\") or {}).keys())\n\n    errors: list[str] = []\n\n    for idx, rule in enumerate(data.get(\"rules\", []), start=1):\n        parts = str(rule).split(\",\")\n        if not parts:\n            continue\n        kind = parts[0]\n        if kind == \"RULE-SET\":\n            if len(parts) < 3:\n                errors.append(f\"rules[{idx}] malformed RULE-SET: {rule}\")\n                continue\n            provider, target = parts[1], parts[2]\n            if provider not in providers:\n                errors.append(f\"rules[{idx}] provider not found: {provider} in {rule}\")\n            if target not in groups and target not in proxies:\n                errors.append(f\"rules[{idx}] target not found: {target} in {rule}\")\n        elif kind in {\"DOMAIN\", \"DOMAIN-SUFFIX\", \"DOMAIN-KEYWORD\", \"IP-CIDR\", \"IP-CIDR6\", \"GEOIP\"}:\n            if len(parts) < 3:\n                errors.append(f\"rules[{idx}] malformed rule: {rule}\")\n                continue\n            target = parts[2]\n            if target not in groups and target not in proxies:\n                errors.append(f\"rules[{idx}] target not found: {target} in {rule}\")\n\n    for group in data.get(\"proxy-groups\", []):\n        if not isinstance(group, dict):\n            continue\n        name = group.get(\"name\", \"<unnamed>\")\n        for ref in group.get(\"proxies\") or []:\n            if ref not in groups and ref not in proxies:\n                errors.append(f\"proxy-group {name!r} references missing proxy/group {ref!r}\")\n\n    print(f\"YAML OK: {p}\")\n    print(f\"proxy-providers: {len(data.get('proxy-providers') or {})}\")\n    print(f\"proxies: {len(data.get('proxies') or [])}\")\n    print(f\"proxy-groups: {len(data.get('proxy-groups') or [])}\")\n    print(f\"rule-providers: {len(data.get('rule-providers') or {})}\")\n    print(f\"rules: {len(data.get('rules') or [])}\")\n\n    if errors:\n        print(\"\\nERRORS:\")\n        for e in errors:\n            print(\"-\", e)\n        return 1\n\n    print(\"reference checks: OK\")\n    return 0\n\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    if len(sys.argv) != 2:\n        print(__doc__.strip(), file=sys.stderr)\n        raise SystemExit(2)\n    raise SystemExit(main(sys.argv[1]))\n", "file_type": ".py"}
